        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271485248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17008953493354304600">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br/><br/>The problem with Angelfire is that it's the type of book that makes you stop in the middle of your reading and say, "Where have I read that before?" It's a mix of multiple ideas, philosophies, and imaginations all rolled into one. For a less prolific reader, I guess this book would come across and stunning and original; however, I found it to be a light and frankly kind of a dull read. <br/><br/>Ellie seems to be normal teenager despite her strange nightmares. It's nearly her seventeenth </span>
  <span id="freeText17008953493354304600" style="display:none">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br /><br />The problem with Angelfire is that it's the type of book that makes you stop in the middle of your reading and say, "Where have I read that before?" It's a mix of multiple ideas, philosophies, and imaginations all rolled into one. For a less prolific reader, I guess this book would come across and stunning and original; however, I found it to be a light and frankly kind of a dull read. <br /><br />Ellie seems to be normal teenager despite her strange nightmares. It's nearly her seventeenth birthday, she's about to get a car, she's hosting a huge party, and her best friend is half in love with her. But, when Ellie's economics teacher is mysteriously murdered and a handsome young man named Will enters her life, everything she's known starts to seem like a lie. Ellie is actually the Preliator, a being with the body of a human yet gifted with unimaginable abilities used for killing demons. Although the Preliator can be killed, they are simply re-born, rotating through multiple lives armed with a Guardian - in Ellie's case, Will. Yet, there is something mysterious about Ellie's abilities. How can Ellie be expected to charge headfirst into her dangerous future, fighting an enemy that is growing stronger with every second, when she can't even unravel her own past? <br /><br />To me, Angelfire seemed like a mix of Cassandra's Clare Mortal Instruments Series, Laini Taylor's Daughter of Smoke and Bone, and Stephanie Meyer's Twilight. There was demon hunting, angelic re-birth/unraveling of a past you couldn't remember, and there was your typical high school setting. Every few chapters or so, Ellie will either (a) meet a reaper who she has to fight (b) sit with Will in the library to do research or (c) be at a party/Movie Night/high school social event. Frankly speaking, it was kind of dull. I'm surprised I even made it through this book. It barely held my attention, the characters were flat, and the writing lacked interest. The only positive qualities that I enjoyed in this book were the fact that Ellie didn't throw herself at Will like most protagonists. Instead, their relationship seemed to be realistic and wasn't too annoying (except for some of their really cliched dialogue). <br /><br />Essentially, Angelfire was an okay read. It had an interesting premises, but since it had been done so many times before in much better ways, it failed to hold my attention. The characters were not particularly unique or wonderful in any way and I was glad to put this book aside when I was done with it. It takes an excruciatingly long time for anything truly interesting to happen, so if I were you, I'd skip out on this one and opt for a more scintillating read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17008953493354304600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_179890737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="John Egbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5223517-john-egbert"><img alt="John Egbert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340483284p2/5223517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179890737" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16109120749882847430">First I was like,<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352172i/705681.png' width='250' height='196' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>But then I was like,<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352172i/705682.jpg' width='215' height='226' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>That's what it was like for me all throughout Angelfire. I kept expecting something awesome and unpredictable to happen, but nothing did. Even when <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Luke found out Darth Vader was his biological father <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I wasn't surprised. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Okay, Luke wasn't <i>really</i> in this book, and neither was Darth Vader, but still. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>The point is that this book was just okay. It wasn't a joyride, but it wasn't a complete snoozefes</span>
  <span id="freeText16109120749882847430" style="display:none">First I was like,<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352172i/705681.png" width="250" height="196" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But then I was like,<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352172i/705682.jpg" width="215" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>That's what it was like for me all throughout Angelfire. I kept expecting something awesome and unpredictable to happen, but nothing did. Even when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Luke found out Darth Vader was his biological father <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I wasn't surprised. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay, Luke wasn't <i>really</i> in this book, and neither was Darth Vader, but still. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The point is that this book was just okay. It wasn't a joyride, but it wasn't a complete snoozefest either (although I did have lots and lots of trouble getting through the beginning). The prose was a little off, and the characters were all flat as cardboard cutouts. Except for Ellie. She was just...unlikable. No offense to her or anything, but I just couldn't really put myself in her position or even side with her.<br><br>Over all, Angelfire was just...<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352172i/705682.jpg" width="215" height="226" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Just okay.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16109120749882847430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_234081496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234081496" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234081496?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Brewer" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer">Annie Brewer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Angel book lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=books-on-my-shelf">books-on-my-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=unbelievable-male-leads">unbelievable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite-hotties">favorite-hotties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=nook-books">nook-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=absolutely-amazingly-awesome">absolutely-amazingly-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234081496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15393327410520674318"><a href='http://s981.photobucket.com/user/goddess793/media/mustread2_zps801c64a8.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362940ra/714150.gif' alt=' photo mustread2_zps801c64a8.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>So. I have a new top favorite angel boyfriend. His name is Will.<br/>Yes, he beats my beloved Patch. <br/>This is my new favorite angel series. I can smell the awesomeness coming in the next two books. <br/>This book was badass! I loved every second of this journey with Ellie to self-discovery when she learns that she's not quite human. She's probably my favorite heroine. She kicks ass. She's strong. She's loyal. She's caring. Overall she's just amazing! <br/><br/>Will, I have no words for this sexy immortal being. </span>
  <span id="freeText15393327410520674318" style="display:none"><a href="http://s981.photobucket.com/user/goddess793/media/mustread2_zps801c64a8.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380362940ra/714150.gif" alt=" photo mustread2_zps801c64a8.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>So. I have a new top favorite angel boyfriend. His name is Will.<br>Yes, he beats my beloved Patch. <br>This is my new favorite angel series. I can smell the awesomeness coming in the next two books. <br>This book was badass! I loved every second of this journey with Ellie to self-discovery when she learns that she's not quite human. She's probably my favorite heroine. She kicks ass. She's strong. She's loyal. She's caring. Overall she's just amazing! <br><br>Will, I have no words for this sexy immortal being. His dark hair and enticing green eyes just sends some major fire straight to my toes. Every time he appeared, my heart did a frickin crazy dance. He's perfectly flawed. He's protective. He's emotional( though he keeps a lot hidden). He's sarcastic. He's swoony, swoony, swoony. He sacrifices himself for his only true love over and over again, putting himself in danger without pause. I love him. I wish I'd met him sooner. But I'm glad to know him now.<br><br>The secondary characters were awesome! I loved Kate and her constant witty banter with Ellie. She's the best kind of best friend. She definitely keeps things interesting. And shes so loyal to Ellie. I like Landon, Chris, Rachel, Evan and all the rest I can't remember. I like her mom, though at first she grated on my nerves. But she's great after all. I HATE her dad with mad passion. What the fuck kind of father calls their daughter worthless? Son of a bitch I was hoping Will would have kicked his ass during one scene. I wanted to jump in and knee him in the balls. What a douche bag!! Also,<br>I love Nathaniel. He's awesome! <br>I was so worried there was a love triangle brewing with Landon and there would have been had she felt the same way. Thank you Ellie for being smart. Thank. You. <br>Now I'm worried about what's to come with Cadan. I don't like him and I know he'll be appearing in the next two books.<br>Hey Cadan, stay the hell away from her!! She belongs with Will!! I'll cut you!<br><br>I hate you Bastian. Ivar. Ragnuk. All you will go to hell. I hope. <br><br>All in all, this book rocked my socks off. It definitely needs more hype. The mythology in the story was amazing. The twists and surprises were holy-shit worthy. It never slowed down. There was constant action in every chapter. I was freaking out, holding my breath, cursing at the book. It rocked! And of course, there was plenty of hot sexual tension. But it wasn't focused solely on that. However, I definitely got my fix for it. And it was good. Holy shit, it was good.<br>But then. Then it was bad. And I was sad. And mad. And I hope to God it gets better. Poor Will. Poor Ellie. Ugh.<br>Anyway, I highly highly recommend this series. I'm so excited to continue this journey with these awesome characters. But it won't be right away, unfortunately. Still, it'll be soon and I can't wait to see where Moulton takes us next. <br><br><br>Okay, so I feel like I didn't write a good enough review for this book. When I finished Angelfall by Susan Ee, I was craving more books like it. I love books with a solid the plot, a world of paranormal creatures, with characters who kick major ass and can still be vulnerable at times, a book with suspense, mystery, edge-of-your-seat-oh-my-god intense moments, and of course...the always needed romance, forbidden in this case. *cries*<br>Well, when picking this up, that's exactly what I got. I got everything I wanted and was looking for. I love the paranormal genre, I love the PNR genre more than the contemporary romance genre. I can't explain it, I just do. Maybe because the authors create such vivid descriptive worlds that we only see in movies. I met Courtney Allison Moulton a few years ago at a book signing. I bought her book, she signed it and then I set it on my bookshelf to read. And I forgot about it. I'm kicking my ass for that now. But when I picked it up to read this weekend, a day ago, two days ago...I don't remember now. But I thought it would be the typical YA PNR story, like all the others. I was so wrong.<br><br>Ellie is a strong and fierce seventeen year old. And she doesn't even know it. Of course, she also doesn't know she's many years older than seventeen. But that's because she doesn't know she's something more than human. And each time she dies in her life, she comes back in the same human body. But on the night of her seventeenth birthday, her life changes in more ways than she's ready to admit. Although, her dreams have become more vivid each night, but now...they're not dreams, they're her reality and she's going to have to face who and what she really is.<br><br>Enter Will. He's someone Ellie knew in her past lives. Someone she's grown close to and eventually her memories of her past comes back to her little by little. Will helps awaken her powers, and helps her learn to fight like the warrior she always was. She's a very important being and she needs to step up and trust Will when he tells her she's the most powerful one of all, and she will need to fight to keep the apocalypse from wiping out the world. It's up to her to save everyone from the creatures that lurk in the darkness, waiting for the right time to kill her. <br><br>All the while still being a regular teenage girl. She's not the most popular, but she's got great supportive friends and everyone likes her. I can't blame them, she's such a likable girl. But it's getting harder to be the person she's always known to be, and yet become the person she was always meant to be. She lies to her friends and parents because while she should be home studying for a test or going out to the mall with Kate, she's with Will fighting the deadliest beings on earth, or in the immortal realm instead and so much destruction happens, innocent people are killed. She's got two very different lives but the way she handles it all is so admirable. I fell in love with both Ellie and Will and loved every second of their story.<br><br>One of my favorite things about this book was the dreams, we got to see what happened in her past lives and who she was fighting. We also got glimpses of Will and Ellie's past life together and it was just beautiful. I loved seeing how they met, who they were and how they've changed. I just love these two so much and I'm so excited to continue this destruction-filled journey with them. I also know there's gonna be much more blood shed and deaths to come and that's gonna be hard to watch. But it's the risk I'm willing to take because I need to know where the next story takes me. I can't wait to see how Moulton weaves Ellie's two separate lives the rest of the books. Will she still be able to live a normal teenage life while fighting the dark side or will her parents-scratch that cause I hate her father to death-her mother find out what she really is?<br><br>Also, I'm anxious to see where Will and Ellie end up, relationship wise. I was very sad and heartbroken at the end of this book because their love is forbidden but I need them to be together. I NEED THEM TO BE TOGETHER! But make no mistake, there was plenty of steamy, passionate moments and I was highly satisfied with that part of the story. Damn, I want a dark haired/green-eyed Guardian named Will. Sigh.<br><br>Anyway, this book was badass and I hope more people will give it a chance. You'll fall in love with this series as quick as I did, I guarentee it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15393327410520674318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9+e/lLEamqWzuu3GSDCe8y6H/Sfv8c3ymPDfw/bgPAvNwdZGCkRTzRSRWae/xZQs+Nga7yF8Q5XDjplyO6POkQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

When she isn't studying ancient civilizations or writing about magic and monsters, she's busy with farm chores. Her debut novel ANGELFIRE was published when she was just 24 years old.<br/><br/>For more information about Courtney, visit her online at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.courtneyallisonmoulton.com'>www.courtneyallisonmoulton.com</a>.</span>
